  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_513328bd-f721-45b4-9f3d-9681e18cd32a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer2957358192360528764">Don’t call them heroes.<br/><br/>But these six Californian teens have powers that set them apart. They can do stuff ordinary people can’t.<br/><br/>Take Ethan, a.k.a. Scam. He’s got a voice inside him that’ll say whatever you want to hear, whether it’s true or not. Which is handy, except when it isn’t—like when the voice starts gabbing in the middle of a bank robbery. The only people who can </span>
  <span id="freeText2957358192360528764" style="display:none">Don’t call them heroes.<br /><br />But these six Californian teens have powers that set them apart. They can do stuff ordinary people can’t.<br /><br />Take Ethan, a.k.a. Scam. He’s got a voice inside him that’ll say whatever you want to hear, whether it’s true or not. Which is handy, except when it isn’t—like when the voice starts gabbing in the middle of a bank robbery. The only people who can help are the other Zeroes, who aren’t exactly best friends these days.<br /><br />Enter Nate, a.k.a. Bellwether, the group’s “glorious leader.” After Scam’s SOS, he pulls the scattered Zeroes back together. But when the rescue blows up in their faces, the Zeroes find themselves propelled into whirlwind encounters with ever more dangerous criminals. And at the heart of the chaos they find Kelsie, who can take a crowd in the palm of her hand and tame it or let it loose as she pleases.<br /><br />Filled with high-stakes action and drama, Zeroes unites three powerhouse authors for the opening installment of a thrilling new series.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/470813-do-people-know-that-is-an-letter">Do people know that &quot;Ø&quot; is an letter, which is used in Denmark and Norwegian?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_470813'><a id="like_count_community_question_470813" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/470813?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F24885636-zeroes">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/470813-do-people-know-that-is-an-letter">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/470813-do-people-know-that-is-an-letter">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/42312395-faranae"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1583105344i/42312395._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/42312395-faranae">Faranae</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Technically, Ø is a different character than the mathematical ∅, but in stylized typography and in handwriting, the difference may be unclear. However<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Technically, Ø is a different character than the mathematical ∅, but in stylized typography and in handwriting, the difference may be unclear. However, here it gets weirder because ∅ means a null set, not zero. The appropriate glyph would be a handwritten slashed zero (where while the slash should remain inside the ellipse, it frequently doesn't). <br /><br />Just for completion's sake, there's also the diameter symbol ⌀.<br /><br /> And these are of course the prescriptivist definitions of these things, which seems to fit the tone of your question better than the descriptivism of Merriam-Webster. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div class='flagAnswer'>
<a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link940158" title="Flag this answer as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=940158&amp;resource_type=CommunityAnswer&amp;return_url=%2Fquestions%2F470813-do-people-know-that-is-an-letter%2Fanswers%2F940158-technically-is-a">flag</a>
</div>
<ul class='communityQAFooter answerFooter'>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330037607" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330037607?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=best-reads-of-2015">best-reads-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330037607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2789265639079821256">It’s always a great experience when you go into a book with no expectations and it turns out you really enjoy it. That’s what happened to me with <i>Zeroes</i> . I hadn’t read a single review beforehand, hadn’t read anything by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13957.Scott_Westerfeld' title='Scott Westerfeld' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scott Westerfeld</a> (though I think I will remedy that now) and have never even heard of the other two authors. <br/><br/>The reason I picked up this book was the premise. I read the summary on Goodreads and was immediately intrigued. I read the tagline and I was even more convinced. If ther</span>
  <span id="freeText2789265639079821256" style="display:none">It’s always a great experience when you go into a book with no expectations and it turns out you really enjoy it. That’s what happened to me with <i>Zeroes</i> . I hadn’t read a single review beforehand, hadn’t read anything by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13957.Scott_Westerfeld" title="Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Scott Westerfeld</a> (though I think I will remedy that now) and have never even heard of the other two authors. <br /><br />The reason I picked up this book was the premise. I read the summary on Goodreads and was immediately intrigued. I read the tagline and I was even more convinced. If there was ever an ultimate tagline to get me hooked <b>“Every Power Has A Price”</b> comes pretty close to it. <br /><br />But we all know the problem with great premises: they easily disappoint. The book sounds better than it actually is. Fortunately, <i>Zeroes</i> doesn’t fall into that category. If you read the summary and are intrigued, if you think it sounds exactly like something you’d love (the way I did), I suggest you pick it up because <b>the story actually delivers on its promise</b>.<br /><br />The story follows six American teenagers who all have some kind of superpower. The powers are all different from one another and so are the kids that have them but for one common attribute: they were all born in the year 2000. These teens have formed a team and call themselves Zeroes (a sarcastic spin on the word “heroes”) and attempt missions to learn more about their powers. The novel begins with the group having split up after they had a falling out the summer before. I’ll let you discover the rest on your own.<br /><br />The problem with superhero stories is that they get old. Kids with superpowers? That has been done countless times before. <b>But <i>Zeroes</i> manages to take an old, worn-out concept and make it into something new, something that I feel like I’ve never read before. The characters in <i>Zeroes</i> are in no sense heroes, they don’t even come close.</b> They’re just a bunch of kids that have been given something they don’t understand and have no idea how to use. This isn’t another coming-of-age story about teens learning to control their power to make the world better. Instead, <b>the novel is very realistic and honest in its portrayal of teenage feelings, desires and morals.</b> None of them are evil but that doesn’t mean they always do the right thing. Quite the opposite actually.<br /><br /><b>What I loved most about this novel is that the authors actually focused on the downsides of having powers instead of the benefits.</b> Here the powers only seem to make the characters’ lives harder, getting them into trouble at every turn, causing fights. All of these powers are incredibly cool and very powerful, yet I realized I wouldn’t really want any of them because the price was just too high. For someone like me who loves magic systems with clear rules and limits this take on the concept was fantastic. I honestly thought authors had already used up all the superpowers there was to draw from but this book proved me wrong. Sure, we’ve all seen the power of persuasion, the power over electronics and the power of invisibility. But trust me, <b>you haven’t seen it done like this</b>. On top of that, the powers were also very consistent and logical which I really appreciated.<br /><br /><b>The novel features a large cast of characters and I found myself really caring about all of them.</b> They were all flawed, had multiple layers to them and complex relationships with one another. I loved that this book had such <b>a heavy emphasis on friendship</b>; I often feel like romantic relationships seem to take over all others in YA. Though the characters weren’t all as fully fleshed out as I would have liked, I can completely understand this since it’s difficult to establish six different characters in one book while still maintaining an engaging plot.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the other elements of the story as well. <b>The novel was very fast-paced and well-written, action-packed as well as humorous.</b> After finishing the book I went on Goodreads and was shocked to find that this novel was 560 pages long. It felt like a much shorter book and didn’t ever drag.<br /><br />There were a few things that could have been better, but nothing that truly lessened my enjoyment of the book. Sometimes the plot felt a little over the top, a little too badass, too dramatic, so that I had some trouble suspending my disbelief. The main problem here is that for some readers this book will feel too juvenile. The insta-love between two certain characters was kind of unnecessary as well and should have been left out, but it took so little page-time that it really didn’t bother me all that much.<br /><br />Overall, I thought this book was excellent. It isn’t my favourite superhero novel (that honour still goes to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious" title="Vicious by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>) but it is certainly up there. If the premise sounds like something you’d enjoy I highly recommend you pick this one up when it comes out on September 29th.<br /><br />Also, dear bookgods, is there any way that this could be made into a TV show? That would make me very, very happy.<br /><br />*thank you to NetGalley for providing me with an eARC of this book*<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2789265639079821256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=writing-i-would-love-to-imitate">writing-i-would-love-to-imitate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330895238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5127024374453540457"><blockquote> <b>“These things we have, they aren’t mental issues; they’re <i>powers.</i> Like superheroes have.”<br/><br/>“You think?”<br/><br/>“Sure. We just suck at them right now.” </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>It is not everyday that you come across a great book without its usual YA tropes plaguing every pages.<br/><br/>Follow by the textbook, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24885636.Zeroes' title='Zeroes by Scott Westerfeld' rel='nofollow noopener'>Zeroes</a> did not. Instead what these three authors do is turn the tables around, thrash all the methodical/formulaic shit there is out there and laugh in the face of clichés and tropes. The end product? <b>
  <i>It’s this.</i>
</b><b> A story so orig</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5127024374453540457" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b>“These things we have, they aren’t mental issues; they’re <i>powers.</i> Like superheroes have.”<br><br>“You think?”<br><br>“Sure. We just suck at them right now.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br>It is not everyday that you come across a great book without its usual YA tropes plaguing every pages.<br><br>Follow by the textbook, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24885636.Zeroes" title="Zeroes by Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Zeroes</a> did not. Instead what these three authors do is turn the tables around, thrash all the methodical/formulaic shit there is out there and laugh in the face of clichés and tropes. The end product? <b>
  <i>It’s this.</i>
</b><b> A story so original, fresh and entertaining as hell.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24885636.Zeroes" title="Zeroes by Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Zeroes</a> is everything that I can ever ask for in a Young Adult book.<br><br>Shove aside the usual superhero powers like invisibility, telepathy or hell, even superhuman strength! What this book has to offer is something else entirely.<br><br>There are 6 teenagers – each with their own uniqueness who know all too well that…<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Every Power Comes With A Price.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>These teens know they’re not normal and what they do can be risky and dangerous to normal civillans. One reckless move and they could jeopardize an entire society. But the thing is… They don’t have big plans to conquer the world or make people bow down to their whims just because they are oh-so-special. They are all about gathering together to learn and to discover what they’re capable of.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Zeroes, not Heroes.”<br></b>
</blockquote><br><br>They don’t have a big agenda set in stones – all they want to do is watch out for each other’s backs and avoid getting in troubles.<br><br>The problem is . . . What they are capable of doing is a magnet for troubles.<br><br>I had so much fun being inside 6 characters’s heads, exploring what they are capable of doing and prying apart their inner thoughts and feelings. <b>You’d be shattered, surprised and awed to learn that their powers almost unmade them in the past. </b>Being different and special is not as glorious as you may think. This may be a story about the impossible, fictional elements but it has a ring of something realistic added to it. I also have so, so much respect for a certain someone who do not misuse/abuse his power just because he can.<br><br><b>When I learned that the book will be told in six different point of views, I was way beyond ecstatic</b>. It was great fun hopping from one different head to the other! <b>Imagine how happy I was when I found out that there is a wide diverse cast here. I was internally squealing FOREVER.</b><br><br>I cannot even gush enough over the writing that is so readable, so easy to process and still so detailed even on the minor things. God, the descriptions are well beyond amazing. The authors even made sure to mention what’s happening in a character’s backgrounds. It made the story read a lot like a movie playing in your head. Though I was expecting the writing to be disjointed since there are 3 authors working on different POVs but to my delight, that balance never shattered nor did the writing ever dragged.<br><br><b>This is just the first book in a trilogy and already I have felt that <i>spark </i>of connection to the many characters here. </b>I feel for them, I root for them, I relate to their teenage thoughts &amp; conflicts, and oh, what the hell? I even swooned for a particular, promising ‘ship’!<br><br>To end this review, I can only say a big profound <b>THANK YOU</b> to Westerfeld, Biancotti and Canagan who helped bring Ethan, Nathan, Thibault, Kelsie, Riley and Chizara to life.<br><br>Seriously, people. Stop reading this review, stop doing whatever it is you are doing – get this book and READ IT.<br><br>As a side note, if you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Victoria%20Schwab" title=" Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener"> Victoria Schwab</a>'s adult psychological superhero book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Vicious___1_" title="Vicious (Vicious, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener"> Vicious</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24885636.Zeroes" title="Zeroes by Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener"> Zeroes</a> is definitely meant for you!<br><br><i> See more reviews at...</i><a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" width="350" height="117" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

  <span id="freeText512426717873098141" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to Simon and Schuster UK Children's and NetGalley.)<br><br><b>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1191648901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191648901" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191648901?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=1">1</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2015">starred-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=aus-nz">aus-nz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191648901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1680738859453593292">The reason I wanted to read this book - Margo Lanagan is a co-author. Unfortunately, I didn't find Lanagan's distinct voice anywhere in Zeroes. Three people had written this novel (although Westerfeld's name is in a much bigger font, why is that?), but all parts of it sounded remarkably similar.<br/><br/>Did I like it overall? It was OK. It's a story about teen heroes with moderately interesting super powers. A lot of action, some romance. Not a bad book, but with not much of a crossover appeal, IMO. Remi</span>
  <span id="freeText1680738859453593292" style="display:none">The reason I wanted to read this book - Margo Lanagan is a co-author. Unfortunately, I didn't find Lanagan's distinct voice anywhere in Zeroes. Three people had written this novel (although Westerfeld's name is in a much bigger font, why is that?), but all parts of it sounded remarkably similar.<br /><br />Did I like it overall? It was OK. It's a story about teen heroes with moderately interesting super powers. A lot of action, some romance. Not a bad book, but with not much of a crossover appeal, IMO. Reminded me a lot of Kelly Armstrong's YA series, from back when I liked her writing.<br /><br />Can't say I am coming back for more. Thankfully, no serious cliffhangers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1680738859453593292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1348391504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1348391504" />
    <a title="joey (thoughts and afterthoughts)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26565437-joey-thoughts-and-afterthoughts"><img alt="joey (thoughts and afterthoughts)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500349319p2/26565437.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1348391504?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="joey (thoughts and afterthoughts)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="joey (thoughts and afterthoughts)" href="/user/show/26565437-joey-thoughts-and-afterthoughts">joey (thoughts and afterthoughts)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26565437-joey-thoughts-and-afterthoughts?shelf=physical-arc">physical-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26565437-joey-thoughts-and-afterthoughts?shelf=arc-review">arc-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1348391504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14324600149196927423"><b>[See the full review at <a href='https://anotherafterthought.wordpress.com/2015/08/26/review-zeroes-westerfeld-lanagan-biancotti/' rel='nofollow noopener'>thoughts and afterthoughts.</a>]</b><br/><br/>I am jello.<br/><br/>Thank you, <i>Bilanafeld...? Westerlanacotti…? (this sounds like manicotti or biscotti--WHATEVER, IT'S NOT THE POINT)</i>--for curing my half a year reading slump. This is my attempt at a ship name for this wonderful trio much like how you gave my favourite ship a name in this book. I also require the sequel. Now would be nice.<br/><a href='https://anotherafterthought.wordpress.com/2015/08/26/review-zeroes-westerfeld-lanagan-biancotti/' rel='nofollow noopener'> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440603929i/15998572._SX540_.png' width='400' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/></a><br/><b>Rating: 4/5</b><br/><b>
  <u>Should this book be picked up? the tl;dr spoiler-less review:</u>
</b><br/>— The superpowers in this story aren’t</span>
  <span id="freeText14324600149196927423" style="display:none"><b>[See the full review at <a href="https://anotherafterthought.wordpress.com/2015/08/26/review-zeroes-westerfeld-lanagan-biancotti/" rel="nofollow noopener">thoughts and afterthoughts.</a>]</b><br><br>I am jello.<br><br>Thank you, <i>Bilanafeld...? Westerlanacotti…? (this sounds like manicotti or biscotti--WHATEVER, IT'S NOT THE POINT)</i>--for curing my half a year reading slump. This is my attempt at a ship name for this wonderful trio much like how you gave my favourite ship a name in this book. I also require the sequel. Now would be nice.<br><a href="https://anotherafterthought.wordpress.com/2015/08/26/review-zeroes-westerfeld-lanagan-biancotti/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440603929i/15998572._SX540_.png" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></a><br><b>Rating: 4/5</b><br><b>
  <u>Should this book be picked up? the tl;dr spoiler-less review:</u>
</b><br>— The superpowers in this story aren’t all otherworldly. There’s a human quality to many of their abilities that exudes a magical realism vibe<br>— Cultural diversity seen through a multi-POV narrative that seamlessly jumps from one voice to another in building perspective<br>— Limited world-building is not problematic as readers are on the same knowledge playing field as the characters themselves<br>— Writing is wonderfully paced; 560-pages feels easy breezy<br>— The romance subplot isn’t too heavy although there’s a cautionary love-v/triangle happening; there are ships you can jump aboard on<br><br><b>
  <u>Initial Thoughts:</u>
</b><br>This book is incredibly fun. I will now proceed to hype this book up.<br><br><i>Full disclosure: I received an advanced reader copy of Zeroes from the Book Blog Ontario Meet-Up. I extend thanks to Simon Pulse for providing me with the opportunity to review this book.</i><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><u><b>Afterthoughts:</b></u><br><br><u><b>Premise</b></u><br>All Ethan “Scam” Cooper wanted was a way home and he was ready to talk up anyone in the vicinity to help him out. But here’s the thing: the voice isn’t always his to speak. It’s his other voice—the one that knows too much and says what others want to hear—who presents Ethan a duffel bag of cash. <i>Finders keepers, right?</i> When he finds himself caught in the middle of a bank robbery, he’ll do whatever it takes to protect what’s his; even if that means calling up his former friends, the Zeroes.<br><br><u><b>Setting</b></u><br>Zeroes is set in sunny Cambria, California during the height of the 4th of July summer festivities. <b>The seaside metropolis is aesthetically accessible</b>—from its pristine glass high-rises to the grungy vacancy of the other side of town—presenting a fictional urban landscape that thrives off the reader’s own local downtown core. <b>Simply put: the world building is smart and aligns itself to fit any environment if you consider the [almost] magical-realism of the superpowers witnessed in the story.</b><br><br><b>The narrative screams urban fantasy with a dabbling of sci-fi even if there isn’t deep context to support the magic systems therein.</b> While this might have been problematic in other worlds, I found this knowledge gap to be welcoming. It works because they’re actively learning the kinks of their own specialness—together—with curiosity, fully knowing that they don’t have all the answers. Exposition, for me, is necessary if history is a requirement as opposed to a fulfillment for storytelling sakes. With readers being along for the journey of experimentalism, the limited scope in setting is a success in its own right.<br><br><u><b>Narration</b></u><br>For many books with one narrative voice (considering superhero-fiction), it becomes easy to disregard the importance of the alternative characters; the supporters merely there to save King/Queen Protagonist. <b>Zeroes displaces that notion by weaving in and out of a six different perspectives</b> (one per main character); <b>each with their own distinct and significant voice. One of the most striking aspects to the writing is when one moment is given visuals through an array of perspectives but never losing the time which continues to tick.</b> It’s what ultimately makes this multi-POV narration seamless and effective. This is propped up by the <b>wicked pacing</b> making this 560-page book read like a breeze; everything is “go, go, go” and credit goes to the conflict itself.<br><br><i>Could the writing have been more purple-prosey?</i> Eh, perhaps.<br><br><i>Would it have demonstrated greater realism if the plotting was executed with truer direct consequence?</i> Yeah, probably.<br><br>But as far as superhero, action-thrillers go, Zeroes subverts the traditional “with great power comes great responsibility” mantra by keeping readers engaged and charmed by its diverse cast and delivers the message “every power has a price” with a one-two punch of teenage awkwardness and the troubling tomfoolery of first-experiences.<br><br><u><b>Characters</b></u><br>The diversity is paramount to the voice in this book. <b>Culturally, there are Latin-Americans (Puerto Ricans, I presume), French, Nigerians, and Russians. Physiologically and mentally, there are twins, the visually impaired, and an almost-self-diagnosed-Schizophrenic, among others.</b> It’s a book brimming with an eclectic cast and all the quirks. I appreciated the complexities in each Zero as they navigated their own emotions and baggage with the outward extroversions and blind trust they had with one another. It’s reflected in the sheer poignancy of the dialogue balanced against the teenage banter in others. I cared for these characters—some more than others—their flaws and how they balanced each other out and sought a sense of purpose; not by codenames and missions, but as friends.<br><br><b>My favourite character is an enigmatic boy named Thibault</b> (alias: Anonymous) who despite being the poster child for Abercrombie and Fitch with his blue eyes and mane of a hairdo, leads a forgotten life. <i>(Note: he’s not actually a model.)</i> Teebo is present but not so; quickly disappearing as he is realized and able to cut the fibers that link himself to the world around him. It’s real sad, but his friendships is quite uplifting, hopeful, and represents the resilience of today’s growing compassion.<br><br><b>I won’t speak much to the romance other than there being both instalust/love and a potential love-V (or triangle) in the works. But what’s important is that it does not eclipse the conflict in the story.</b><br><br><u><b>Overall</b></u><br>While this story is co-authored, there’s no evident divergence in writing style to really delineate who wrote what. <b>For me, the dialogue and often stark humour flowed, the writing was epically paced, the action never lost its momentum, and the feels were fucking unreal. It was a tight reading experience; a wild joyride and perhaps one of the better releases I’ve read in 2015.</b> Yeah there are issues with contextual world-building but they’re avenues of future exploration.<br><br>Westerfeld, Lanagan, and Biancotti have crafted an unputdownable story that could translate well on the small stage (I’m thinking Nickelodeon) and <b>though you might come for the urban fantasy and the superpowers, you definitely stay for the characters and the remarkable undertones of realistic fiction (or perhaps magical realism) that runs deep in this story.</b><br><br><b>[See the full review at <a href="https://anotherafterthought.wordpress.com/2015/08/26/review-zeroes-westerfeld-lanagan-biancotti/" rel="nofollow noopener">thoughts and afterthoughts.</a>]</b><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14324600149196927423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478226398" />
    <a title="Taylor Knight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight"><img alt="Taylor Knight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536879168p2/12627819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1478226398?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor Knight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor Knight" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight">Taylor Knight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1478226398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5125494821988916088">I wasn't sure what to expect with this book but when I read the publisher's description, I got really pumped. "Filled with high-stakes action and drama" really caught my attention. I shouldn't have got my hopes high but I did. And I was left disappointed.<br/>I really like the concept of this book and the writing was pretty good but what really got me was all the different perspectives and how long it took to set up each character. It jumped from character to character and nothing really set them apa</span>
  <span id="freeText5125494821988916088" style="display:none">I wasn't sure what to expect with this book but when I read the publisher's description, I got really pumped. "Filled with high-stakes action and drama" really caught my attention. I shouldn't have got my hopes high but I did. And I was left disappointed.<br />I really like the concept of this book and the writing was pretty good but what really got me was all the different perspectives and how long it took to set up each character. It jumped from character to character and nothing really set them apart so at times I forgot who's perspective I was reading from. I felt like at least 200 pages of this book was introducing the characters. I personally think that the character's perspectives should have been introduced like The Lunar Chronicles, a new perspective each book. <br />I was really overwhelmed with the info dumping for the first 200-ish pages as well. And because of that, I got a little bored. <br />Overall, this was a fun book and I did like it but it wasn't one of my favorites. If you're looking for a book with superheroes, I think this would a good one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5125494821988916088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8205382461258906631"><b>5 Words: powers, friends, family, attraction, saving-the-world.</b><br/><br/>This was an OK read.<br/><br/>It was interesting, but the pace fluctuated too much for me. It didn't keep me hooked, I feel that it peaked too soon.<br/><br/>I didn't really click with any of the characters, I didn't get on with them. And I found that I didn't want to.<br/><br/>And I so badly wanted the author to be brave and kill off certain characters, it would have made this book so much stronger.   <span id="freeText8205382461258906631" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: powers, friends, family, attraction, saving-the-world.</b><br /><br />This was an OK read.<br /><br />It was interesting, but the pace fluctuated too much for me. It didn't keep me hooked, I feel that it peaked too soon.<br /><br />I didn't really click with any of the characters, I didn't get on with them. And I found that I didn't want to.<br /><br />And I so badly wanted the author to be brave and kill off certain characters, it would have made this book so much stronger. But it's going to be part of a series, so obviously there can't be deaths at this point. That's just not done.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this for free via NetGalley for review purposes.</i></span>

<div id="review_1417205940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1417205940" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14066678-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481826762p2/14066678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1417205940?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/14066678-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14066678-christina?shelf=dnf-didn-t-care-for-skimmed-through">dnf-didn-t-care-for-skimmed-through</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1417205940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4289551987328729602"><b>DNF @ 33%</b><br/><br/>This was my first Scott Westerfeld novel. That being said, I'm not in too much of a hurry to try out his others. The idea for the novel really caught my attention. <br/><br/>Six California teens that have powers that set them apart from everyone else:<br/><br/><i>Scam-</i> the voice inside him says whatever you want to hear<br/><i>Crash-</i> brings technology to its knees<br/><i>Flicker-</i> can see through anyone's eyes but her own<br/><i>Anonymous-</i> out of sight, out of mind<br/><i>Bellwether-</i> Focuses the energy of the group on one goal<br/>and the sixth <i>-</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4289551987328729602" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 33%</b><br /><br />This was my first Scott Westerfeld novel. That being said, I'm not in too much of a hurry to try out his others. The idea for the novel really caught my attention. <br /><br />Six California teens that have powers that set them apart from everyone else:<br /><br /><i>Scam-</i> the voice inside him says whatever you want to hear<br /><i>Crash-</i> brings technology to its knees<br /><i>Flicker-</i> can see through anyone's eyes but her own<br /><i>Anonymous-</i> out of sight, out of mind<br /><i>Bellwether-</i> Focuses the energy of the group on one goal<br />and the sixth <i>- Kelsie -</i> not yet a party of their group, but definitely getting entangled. She can control the emotions of a crowd.<br /><br />Ethan (Scam) has got a voice that will say whatever you want to hear, whether it's true or not. It can be handy, or can land him in a world of trouble...like when the voice starts gabbing in the middle of a bank robbery and lands him in deep. The only people who can help are the other Zeroes, who aren't really on speaking terms anymore.<br />Enter Nate (Bellwether), the group's "glorious leader". After Scam's SOS, he pulls the scattered Zeroes back together. But when the rescue blows up in their faces, the Zeroes find themselves propelled into whirlwind encounters with ever more dangerous criminals across the city.<br /><br />So basically every problem thus far in this book, was because Ethan is a selfish idiot. The reason the Zeroes were no longer friends? Because of Ethan apparently saying some hurtful things to the others with "the voice". The reason he was at the bank during the robbery? Because he had basically stolen a large duffel bag of money from a drug dealer while attempting to get a ride home and decided he had earned that money. The reason the rescue plan went to hell? Because he panicked after using "the voice" on the bank robber and getting detained by the police for questioning and had to send out a request for help. Ethan was pissing me off. <br /><br />It's funny, usually in YA, I find the characters to be more mature than their age would suggest, but it was the opposite with this one. I couldn't imagine finishing out this book, which still had over 300 pages left in it. I've got too many other (hopefully better) books waiting to be read, so this one's going back to the library and maybe the next person to check it out will get more out of it than I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4289551987328729602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1455153037" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455153037" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49090711-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519872099p2/49090711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455153037?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/49090711-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49090711-megan?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49090711-megan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49090711-megan?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49090711-megan?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455153037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9199475745300656485">First things first I love superheroes. I adore them. So when I heard that Scott Westerfield had co-written a nearly 600 page book about kids with super powers I was down. I was so down. Young Avengers and Teen Titans is my jam.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, Zeroes is not my jam. It is not my peanut butter either.<br/><br/>I’ve read a lot of Scott Westerfeld. Back in Junior High I went through a bit of a phase where I just read everything of his, so when I saw his name splashed across the cover I was sure I’d like Zeroes.</span>
  <span id="freeText9199475745300656485" style="display:none">First things first I love superheroes. I adore them. So when I heard that Scott Westerfield had co-written a nearly 600 page book about kids with super powers I was down. I was so down. Young Avengers and Teen Titans is my jam.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Zeroes is not my jam. It is not my peanut butter either.<br /><br />I’ve read a lot of Scott Westerfeld. Back in Junior High I went through a bit of a phase where I just read everything of his, so when I saw his name splashed across the cover I was sure I’d like Zeroes. Maybe I should re-read some past Westerfeld works and see if they really were worth all that noise because <i>Zeroes</i> is just...meh. <br /><br />Zeroes is okay. For me it was a solid 2.5/5 stars and that’s it. It doesn't feel special, it's your typical action movie/superhero plot except none of the bad guys have powers and the characters never come across as being in actual danger. Throw in some cliche romance (in the book’s defense, the romance was barely there) and I am done. <br /><br />At times the plot felt like it was moving along too fast. Just 2 days and Anonymous and Scam are BFF’s? Flicker takes one look at Anonymous (tall, dark, handsome), decides he’s the most beautiful boy she’s ever seen and decides she’ll stalk him back to his house? It's little forced (after a while their little romance felt kind of cute but still... annoying)<br /><br />I don't understand why the Zeroes completely broke up in the first place, either. A group of super-powered teenagers find each other and then split over some cruel words? It feels weak.<br /><br />On the upside, their powers are original and interesting. It’s hard to find a comic / book that doesn’t recycle the same “special abilities” over and over again. The character cast is diverse (racially, economically,and disability wise). I felt for Anonymous and wanted to know more about him. Scam on the other hand was an absolute idiot. Just completely. Despite that I couldn’t bring myself to hate him, I even feel sorry for him. At least dye your hair dude! Wear some sunglasses! Maybe a hat! You literally have gangsters after you some self-preservation would be nice.<br /><br /><br /><br />Plot: 2/5<br />Characters: 2.5/5<br />Writing: 3/5<br />Pacing: 2.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="9199475745300656485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1629634938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1629634938" />
    <a title="Pinky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky"><img alt="Pinky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489855494p2/27523984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1629634938?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pinky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pinky" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky">Pinky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27523984-pinky?shelf=books-i-want-to-own">books-i-want-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629634938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10056853061351034606"> It took me awhile to read this but it was amazing! I loved it so much, it was a lot of fun to read. There was so much action and I couldn't stop reading, even though I was interrupted a bunch of times. :( The struggles of being a reader! Anyway, I am so glad I picked this up, I was at the library and saw this and grabbed it! <br/><br/> <i>
  <b>“Wisdom tells me I'm nothing, love tells me I'm everything.”</b>
</i><br/><br/> This book follows 6 teenagers who have a life that is nothing near ordinary. They all have a power, but ea</span>
  <span id="freeText10056853061351034606" style="display:none"> It took me awhile to read this but it was amazing! I loved it so much, it was a lot of fun to read. There was so much action and I couldn't stop reading, even though I was interrupted a bunch of times. :( The struggles of being a reader! Anyway, I am so glad I picked this up, I was at the library and saw this and grabbed it! <br><br> <i>
  <b>“Wisdom tells me I'm nothing, love tells me I'm everything.”</b>
</i><br><br> This book follows 6 teenagers who have a life that is nothing near ordinary. They all have a power, but each power comes with a price. Scam has the voice, which says what he wants to hear but gets him into sticky situations. It also follows many others like Crash, Bellweather, Flicker, Mob, and Anonymous. They call themselves zeros, those who aren't heroes. After an incident in the summer, the zeros separated. But the zeros are forced to work together after Scam was taken by the cops because of a bank robbery. The adventure starts to unfold, showing the characters go through crazy adventures.<br><br> <i>
  <b>“No one owns the sunset,” </b>
</i><br><br> I loved this book so much, it had the perfect amount of humor and action. It was so much fun to read, there was so much that happened, I never got time to recover from what had happened because more things were thrown at me. It was like a roller-coaster with a bunch of loops that won't stop until the very end. And in order to stay on this roller-coaster, you have to hold on tight! And that's what I did the entire time I was reading, I was holding the book with a death-grip.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462926879ra/19061654.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> The characters were a lot of fun to read about, each one was unique in their own way. I loved the small inside jokes they had and how they had each other's back. My least favourite zero would be Scam, I am not a huge fan of his character, I like the voice but it's scary at how much it knows. Flicker is cool, but I wanted to learn more about her. Anonymous had a very sad past and he has the most difficult power to deal with. Bellweather was cool and kept the group together. I like Crash a lot, she was so cool! Mob was interesting but really selfish. But these guys make an awesome squad! <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462926704ra/19061624.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> The bonds between the different characters was cool to see. I loved Anonymous and Flicker, they were awesome and the way their relationship progressed was cool. It must be painful for Anonymous though, his power is so hard to deal with. Scam's relationship with everyone is uneasy but I am glad to see it progress slowly into something different. Crash is a great friend and I love all of the character development in this book! <br><br> The book pacing was super fast, it felt like I was going crazy! There are so many things that happen and all of the things that happen are so unexpected. I went into this book thinking that it would be about a bunch of heros who are living a double life. I didn't even read the summary of the book I just dove in and it was so different. The different point of views fit the pacing of this book! Each character felt different because of how good the writing was! I can differentiate the different character's voices because of how well the writing was. <br><br> I highly recommend this book to anyone who wants a big adventure filled with twists an turns. Anyone who is ready to jump on a roller-coaster, should read this book! It's one thing that you shouldn't be missing out on! <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10056853061351034606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1398060173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1398060173" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483254339p2/2917700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1398060173?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925266955" href="/book/show/24756394-zeroes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=loveozya">loveozya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398060173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13402030997904487542">Damn that was an enjoyable ride!<br/><br/>The Zeroes are six not-so-normal teenagers, all born in the year 2000, all with some social-related super power. There are way too many main characters for me to talk about them in minute detail, so instead here are some brief dot points:<br/><br/>- Nate (a.k.a. <i>Bellwether</i>, a.k.a. <i>Glorious Leader</i>) has the ability to bend crowds to his will. He can make them focus in on him, believe him, trust him. Comes in handy considering his aspirations to become a politician. <br/><br/>- Ethan (a</span>
  <span id="freeText13402030997904487542" style="display:none">Damn that was an enjoyable ride!<br /><br />The Zeroes are six not-so-normal teenagers, all born in the year 2000, all with some social-related super power. There are way too many main characters for me to talk about them in minute detail, so instead here are some brief dot points:<br /><br />- Nate (a.k.a. <i>Bellwether</i>, a.k.a. <i>Glorious Leader</i>) has the ability to bend crowds to his will. He can make them focus in on him, believe him, trust him. Comes in handy considering his aspirations to become a politician. <br /><br />- Ethan (a.k.a. <i>Scam</i>) has another voice inside him. All he has to do is open his mouth and The Voice will say whatever is necessary to achieve Ethan’s goals - whether that be to be left alone, which consequently fucked up his relationship with the Zeroes a year prior - or to get a ride home - leading us to the events of this awesome book. He was a fairly whiny character, always letting The Voice speak for him when times get tough and yet never taking responsibility for what The Voice says.<br /><br />- Riley (a.k.a. <i>Flicker</i>) is blind, but not really. Riley has the very interesting ability to “see” through other people’s eyes. Isn’t that the coolest? She has a very interesting link with her twin sister - I get the feeling she’s a Zero in some way, too.<br /><br />- Chizara (a.k.a. <i>Crash</i>) has an itch that can only be scratched by “crashing” all surrounding technology. The buzz of electricity burrow under her skin and won’t leave her be. I think Chizara was one of the most interesting of the Zeroes. She was painfully aware of just how horrible their powers can become; she’s not sure if she even wants to be a Zero in the first place. I seriously enjoyed her character progression in this one and can’t wait to see more of it in the next two books.<br /><br />- Kelsie (a.k.a. <i>Mob</i>) has a similar crowd-related power to Bellwether, except instead of controlling the crowd, the crowd becomes a single entity for her to affect. Whether that be by making them dance the night away or by making them fearful. I’m still really intrigued about her character; can’t wait to see her grow in the rest of the series.<br /><br />- Thibault (a.k.a. <i>Anonymous</i>) has the most heartbreaking of all the powers. Thibault is “anonymous” with a crowd (i.e. more than five people), in the sense that people forget he’s there. Even his own family. *Cue heartbreak here*.<br /><br />All of their powers - except for Ethan’s - work on a curve, which I found to be super interesting. Basically, although Ethan’s powers only really work one-on-one, the other Zeroes' powers work best when there are in a group of at least six people. What makes this number so special? I hope we’ll find out.<br /><br />The cultural diversity in this novel was awesome. Bellwether is Hispanic and Chizara is of African-descent (forgive me for not being able to pinpoint exactly where). I could do with a little more LGBTA+ representation but I’m pretty happy with what we have so far.<br /><br />Although each author wrote 2 characters, it flowed seemlessly. Usually with such a large ensemble, there is always a character whose POV I hate having to plow through, but that was not the case with Zeroes. I found each and every character to be interesting in their own right. <br /><br />The plot was fairly fast paced and action-oriented. Which is strange considering that this first instalment takes place over the course of two weeks. The ending was good, but could have been better. I found it to be the perfect set-up for more to come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13402030997904487542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The writing was sharp and beautiful.<br/><br/>I feel like super-heroes are big right now, so much so that it's hard to differentiate between them and get excited about another superhero story. But this book offered a lot. Great descriptive lines, and highly imaginative. <br/><br/>Highly recommend! </span>

<div id="review_1283384556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283384556" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283384556?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283384556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2082392683716493781">Zeroes is the first in a new YA superhero trilogy written by heavy-hitters Scott Westerfeld, Margo Lanagan and Deborah Biancotti.<br/><br/>In it, six teenagers, all born in the same year of 2000, have superpowers. They are the “zeroes”, brought together by their Glorious Leader Nate (or “Bellwether”), an ambitious young man who has a vision for the group and had been trying to train and develop their abilities. Then, one year before the story starts, Ethan/”Scam” torn them apart with the truths no one dar</span>
  <span id="freeText2082392683716493781" style="display:none">Zeroes is the first in a new YA superhero trilogy written by heavy-hitters Scott Westerfeld, Margo Lanagan and Deborah Biancotti.<br /><br />In it, six teenagers, all born in the same year of 2000, have superpowers. They are the “zeroes”, brought together by their Glorious Leader Nate (or “Bellwether”), an ambitious young man who has a vision for the group and had been trying to train and develop their abilities. Then, one year before the story starts, Ethan/”Scam” torn them apart with the truths no one dared to say out loud. Now Scam is in trouble: the “voice” that speaks on his behalf once more speaks truths but this time, to the wrong people. With both criminals and the police after him, he has no one to turn to but the zeroes. And they come to the rescue. Like a well-oiled machine they get him out and to safety but when doing so, start a chain events that could prove fatal.<br /><br />And then they find another unknown zero out there.<br /><br />Zeroes is a character piece: the characters’ motivations and inner conflict move the story along and the chapters alternate, with viewpoints from all six characters. I understand that each author is responsible for two out of six (but no one knows who writes who). An aside: it’s difficult to differentiate each of the characters’ voices and I’d be hard press to even start guessing who wrote what. I wonder: does this mean the book is seamlessly edited? Or that it is far too edited to make each individual voice sound pretty much the same?<br /><br />Digression aside, Zeroes deals with superpowers that are less flashy and cool and more… subtle, double-edged, inconvenient and often downright awful. Take for example Anonymous: who can disappear so easily that everybody has problems remembering him – even his own family. Mob, who can control the feeling and moods of a crowd but also be overwhelmed by them and when negative feelings are enhanced, things can definitely turn to worse. Crash, who can literally crash all electronics but who finds it hard to control her power and could potentially destroy entire communication nets – not to mention the ill-feeling she has whenever near that “noise”. Or Flicker who is blind but can see through everybody’s eyes (apart from Anonymous’ for some reason): if you think this is a disgusting invasion of privacy: YOU ARE CORRECT.<br /><br />Most powers here – especially Flicker’s, Mob’s, Scam and Bellwether’s are about controlling/affecting other people – their feelings, their mood, their eyes and their reactions. The moral and ethics of this is a recurring element for some of them but mostly, these teenagers – especially Nate – are incredibly self-centred and lacking empathy.<br /><br />Zeroes, AKA Assholes.<br /><br />I kid, of course. The point of the novel – and I am guessing of the entire trilogy – is that journey of moving away from being stupid idiots to worthy members of society. I love superhero stories exactly because of that: because powers are often double-edged swords that can cut both ways but we don’t see that conundrum enough. In this first book, it is Crash – whose power increases and changes and morphs more than anybody else’s that really undergoes that journey. I love that sense of moral and ethics is fuelled by her mother. It’s not for nothing that the subheading of the novel is “Every power has a price”.<br /><br />Now, doesn’t this sound awesome? Add to that the fact that the cast of characters is racially diverse (Nate is a super wealthy latino, we really don’t see that a lot in books) and that there is one cute romance that develops between two unexpected characters and you have the potential for GREATNESS.<br /><br />But for all of this, Zeroes is so just so very bland. There are sparks here and there: Anonymous’ narrative and very presence in the novel adds a level of unreliability because people have such a hard time remembering him and his story is by far the most emotionally engaging. The flashy side of Crash’s power increases the cool factor. But mostly, the narrative feels repetitive and overlong, going round in circles of sameness especially regarding the characters’ inner conflicts.<br /><br />At the end of the day, Zeroes was an ok read – with really great, fun parts but underwhelming on the whole. Given the premise and the authors involved, I am afraid I was expecting a lot more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2082392683716493781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1388211923" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1388211923" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1388211923?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925266955" href="/book/show/24756394-zeroes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=to-review">to-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1388211923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12178060847144327587">This review appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2016/11/07/zero-swarm-reviews-superhero-misfits-meet-match/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>! Check it out for more reviews.<br/><br/>Superheroes are my jam and Zeroes is a high octane, action-packed story about a team of teenage misfits who also happen to have powers.<br/><br/>Superpowers never get old for me, and I loved hearing about the different powers that each of the six teens had. Kelsie has the power of crowd control, which comes in handy in dangerous public situations. Scam has an all knowing, all seeing voice that gets him in – and out of situations in a j</span>
  <span id="freeText12178060847144327587" style="display:none">This review appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2016/11/07/zero-swarm-reviews-superhero-misfits-meet-match/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>! Check it out for more reviews.<br /><br />Superheroes are my jam and Zeroes is a high octane, action-packed story about a team of teenage misfits who also happen to have powers.<br /><br />Superpowers never get old for me, and I loved hearing about the different powers that each of the six teens had. Kelsie has the power of crowd control, which comes in handy in dangerous public situations. Scam has an all knowing, all seeing voice that gets him in – and out of situations in a jiffy without much control over what he says. Anonymous seems to fade from existence as people easily forget about him. There’s also Nate, or the Glorious Leader who can control people’s reactions to him and Flicker, the blind girl who can see from people’s eyes. Each of their powers were interesting and fun to read about, as they used them as the story unfolded.<br /><br />With so many point of views, the one who I was most fascinated with was Ethan aka Scam. It was interesting how his power was compared to schizophrenia, as he doesn’t have control over the ‘voice’ that somehow knows things about people that only they know. It was fascinating seeing the shift in his demeanour – from the geeky, unconfident teenager to the confident, charismatic person while his voice was in use. It would actually be pretty freaky – and amazing – seeing that change in someone, especially when he starts manipulating siutations from his very emotions.<br /><br />There isn’t much background for each of the characters, and we aren’t given how they got the powers to begin with. Is this a natural phenomenon, are they the only ones with powers, or is it some sort of hidden code between them? When it comes to the validity of the world being built, answering these questions is important, and I hope it’s addressed in the sequel, Swarm. There also isn’t much of a plot line, with most of the story focused on unfolding current events and saving Kelsie’s dad. Who are the Zeroes, what are Nate’s plans for them and what do they usually do with themselves? I have so many questions, and not enough answers.<br /><br />As an action-packed superhero read, Zeroes definitely fits the bill when it comes to superpowers and fun. Each of the characters are fun and unique, especially when discovering what they have to offer the group. The book doesn’t give a lot of depth or background when it comes to the characters or where the powers came from however, so it’s best enjoyed without thinking too much about it.<br /><br /><i>I received a review copy in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_1322323049" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1322323049" />
    <a title="Emma Sea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5558652-emma-sea"><img alt="Emma Sea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458168141p2/5558652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322323049?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Sea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Sea" href="/user/show/5558652-emma-sea">Emma Sea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5558652-emma-sea?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322323049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16322062030232127257">Bailed at page 127, when I realized I was saddened by the thought of having to pick this up again. <br/><br/>I've been a giant Westerfeld fan, and, although I don't think I even made it to the second act, the setup was masterfully written. Smooth as fuck, man. I just couldn't connect with the characters. I don't know, did I grow out of YA? I'm an old, so . . . I guess so? <br/><br/>Sad panda.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
